Practice Ladder - Creating a StoreGuided Practice

Create a theme/settings store with actions to update preferences.

Global state is useful only when multiple unrelated parts of the app need the same client-side data. Before using a store, ask whether the state should be local, lifted to a parent, represented in the URL, or owned by the server cache.

StateBest homeExample
Open modalLocal componentuseState(false)
Selected dashboard filterURL/search params?status=open
Theme preferenceGlobal storeuseSettingsStore()
Fetched postsReact QueryuseQuery()
js — stores/useTodoStore.js
import { create } from 'zustand'

const useTodoStore = create((set, get) => ({
  // State
  todos: [],
  filter: 'all',  // 'all' | 'active' | 'done'

  // Actions
  addTodo: (text) =>
    set(state => ({
      todos: [...state.todos, { id: Date.now(), text, done: false }]
    })),

  toggleTodo: (id) =>
    set(state => ({
      todos: state.todos.map(t =>
        t.id === id ? { ...t, done: !t.done } : t
      )
    })),

  deleteTodo: (id) =>
    set(state => ({
      todos: state.todos.filter(t => t.id !== id)
    })),

  setFilter: (filter) => set({ filter }),

  // Computed (derived) value using get()
  getFiltered: () => {
    const { todos, filter } = get()
    if (filter === 'active') return todos.filter(t => !t.done)
    if (filter === 'done') return todos.filter(t => t.done)
    return todos
  }
}))

export default useTodoStore

Using the Store in Components

Purpose, From First Principles

Why it exists

Store usage exists to connect components to shared state and actions.

What if it did not exist?

Without careful usage, components either cannot access shared state or re-render more than needed.

Learning Ladder

Beginner

Read a value and call an action from the store.

Intermediate

Select only the state a component needs.

Advanced

Avoid deriving expensive values inside many components repeatedly.

Mastery

Keep components expressive: UI describes what it needs, store owns how state changes.

Why It Exists - Detailed Explanation

Store usage exists to connect components to shared state and actions. In a real project, this concept gives a name and a repeatable pattern to a problem you will meet many times. Beginners should first connect the concept to a concrete pain: repeated code, unsafe changes, unclear data flow, hard-to-share screens, or unreliable releases. Once that pain is visible, the feature stops feeling like syntax and starts feeling like a tool.

Practice Ladder - Using the Store in ComponentsGuided Practice

Build a counter store and use it from a header, sidebar, and main panel.

jsx — TodoApp.jsx
import { useState } from 'react'
import useTodoStore from './stores/useTodoStore'

function TodoInput() {
  const [text, setText] = useState('')
  const addTodo = useTodoStore(state => state.addTodo)

  const submit = (e) => {
    e.preventDefault()
    if (!text.trim()) return
    addTodo(text.trim())
    setText('')
  }

  return (
    <form onSubmit={submit}>
      <input value={text} onChange={e => setText(e.target.value)} placeholder="New todo..." />
      <button type="submit">Add</button>
    </form>
  )
}

function TodoList() {
  const { getFiltered, toggleTodo, deleteTodo } = useTodoStore()

  return (
    <ul>
      {getFiltered().map(todo => (
        <li key={todo.id} style={{ textDecoration: todo.done ? 'line-through' : 'none' }}>
          <input type="checkbox" checked={todo.done} onChange={() => toggleTodo(todo.id)} />
          {todo.text}
          <button onClick={() => deleteTodo(todo.id)}>×</button>
        </li>
      ))}
    </ul>
  )
}

function FilterBar() {
  const { filter, setFilter } = useTodoStore()
  return (
    <div>
      {['all', 'active', 'done'].map(f => (
        <button key={f} onClick={() => setFilter(f)}
          style={{ fontWeight: filter === f ? 'bold' : 'normal' }}>
          {f}
        </button>
      ))}
    </div>
  )
}

export function TodoApp() {
  return (
    <div>
      <TodoInput />
      <FilterBar />
      <TodoList />
    </div>
  )
}

Persisting State with Zustand Middleware

Purpose, From First Principles

Why it exists

Persistence exists to keep selected client state after refresh, like theme, sidebar state, or draft preferences.

What if it did not exist?

Without persistence, users lose harmless preferences every time the page reloads.

Learning Ladder

Beginner

Persist small non-sensitive values.

Intermediate

Choose which fields should persist and which should reset.

Advanced

Handle migrations when persisted state shape changes.

Mastery

Persist intentionally; never store secrets or server-owned truth blindly.

Why It Exists - Detailed Explanation

Persistence exists to keep selected client state after refresh, like theme, sidebar state, or draft preferences. In a real project, this concept gives a name and a repeatable pattern to a problem you will meet many times. Beginners should first connect the concept to a concrete pain: repeated code, unsafe changes, unclear data flow, hard-to-share screens, or unreliable releases. Once that pain is visible, the feature stops feeling like syntax and starts feeling like a tool.

Example: when working with Persisting State with Zustand Middleware, look for the smallest situation where the idea removes confusion or prevents a bug.

example

What If It Did Not Exist? - Detailed Explanation

Without persistence, users lose harmless preferences every time the page reloads. This does not always mean the app is impossible to build. Exercise 8.1 — Cart with Zustand Day 8 · Exercise 1

Migrate the Day 4 shopping cart to Zustand. The store should support: adding items (with quantity), removing items, updating quantity, and computing a total. The cart count should show in a navbar that's in a completely separate component.

js — stores/useCartStore.js
import { create } from 'zustand'

const useCartStore = create((set, get) => ({
  items: [],

  addItem: (product) => set(state => {
    const existing = state.items.find(i => i.id === product.id)
    if (existing) {
      return { items: state.items.map(i =>
        i.id === product.id ? { ...i, qty: i.qty + 1 } : i
      )}
    }
    return { items: [...state.items, { ...product, qty: 1 }] }
  }),

  removeItem: (id) =>
    set(state => ({ items: state.items.filter(i => i.id !== id) })),

  getTotal: () =>
    get().items.reduce((sum, i) => sum + i.price * i.qty, 0),

  getCount: () =>
    get().items.reduce((sum, i) => sum + i.qty, 0),
}))
export default useCartStore

// Navbar — reads count from store without props
function Navbar() {
  const getCount = useCartStore(s => s.getCount)
  return <nav>My Store <span>🛒 {getCount()}</span></nav>
}

What if it did not exist?

Practice Ladder - Axios — HTTP ClientGuided Practice

Create an API client and fetch a list of posts with retry/error UI.

API work is not just "fetch and display." Real interfaces need loading states, error states, empty states, retries, pagination, caching, and a way to keep old data visible while new data loads.

API UI State Pattern

jsx
if (isLoading) return <LoadingSkeleton />
if (isError) return <RetryMessage onRetry={refetch} />
if (posts.length === 0) return <EmptyState />

return <PostList posts={posts} isRefreshing={isFetching} />
bash
npm install axios
js — api/client.js
import axios from 'axios'

// Create a configured instance
const api = axios.create({
  baseURL: 'https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com',
  timeout: 10000,
  headers: { 'Content-Type': 'application/json' }
})

// Request interceptor — add auth token
api.interceptors.request.use(config => {
  const token = localStorage.getItem('token')
  if (token) config.headers.Authorization = `Bearer ${token}`
  return config
})

// Response interceptor — handle errors globally
api.interceptors.response.use(
  response => response.data,
  error => {
    if (error.response?.status === 401) {
      // Redirect to login
      window.location.href = '/login'
    }
    return Promise.reject(error)
  }
)

export default api
js — api/posts.js
import api from './client'

export const postsApi = {
  getAll: () => api.get('/posts'),
  getById: (id) => api.get(`/posts/${id}`),
  create: (data) => api.post('/posts', data),
  update: (id, data) => api.put(`/posts/${id}`, data),
  patch: (id, data) => api.patch(`/posts/${id}`, data),
  delete: (id) => api.delete(`/posts/${id}`),
}

TanStack Query (React Query)

Practice Ladder - TanStack Query (React Query)Guided Practice

Fetch posts, view details, create a post, and invalidate the list after success.

React Query handles caching, background refetching, loading/error states, and much more — making async state management effortless.

bash
npm install @tanstack/react-query
jsx — main.jsx
import { QueryClient, QueryClientProvider } from '@tanstack/react-query'
import { ReactQueryDevtools } from '@tanstack/react-query-devtools'

const queryClient = new QueryClient({
  defaultOptions: {
    queries: {
      staleTime: 1000 * 60 * 5,  // 5 minutes
      retry: 2,
    }
  }
})

ReactDOM.createRoot(document.getElementById('root')).render(
  <QueryClientProvider client={queryClient}>
    <App />
    <ReactQueryDevtools initialIsOpen={false} />
  </QueryClientProvider>
)
jsx — PostList.jsx
import { useQuery, useMutation, useQueryClient } from '@tanstack/react-query'
import { postsApi } from './api/posts'

function PostList() {
  const queryClient = useQueryClient()

  // Fetching
  const { data: posts, isLoading, error } = useQuery({
    queryKey: ['posts'],
    queryFn: postsApi.getAll,
  })

  // Mutation (create)
  const createPost = useMutation({
    mutationFn: postsApi.create,
    onSuccess: () => {
      // Invalidate cache — triggers refetch
      queryClient.invalidateQueries({ queryKey: ['posts'] })
    }
  })

  if (isLoading) return <p>Loading...</p>
  if (error) return <p>Error: {error.message}</p>

  return (
    <div>
      <button
        onClick={() => createPost.mutate({ title: 'New Post', body: 'Content', userId: 1 })}
        disabled={createPost.isPending}
      >
        {createPost.isPending ? 'Creating...' : 'Create Post'}
      </button>
      {posts?.slice(0, 5).map(p => (
        <div key={p.id}><strong>{p.title}</strong></div>
      ))}
    </div>
  )
}
Exercise 9.1 — Paginated Posts Day 9 · Exercise 1

Build a paginated post browser using React Query. Show 5 posts per page with Previous/Next buttons. Prefetch the next page when on the current page for instant navigation.

jsx
import { useState } from 'react'
import { useQuery, useQueryClient } from '@tanstack/react-query'
import axios from 'axios'

const fetchPosts = async (page) => {
  const { data } = await axios.get(
    `https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/posts?_page=${page}&_limit=5`
  )
  return data
}

function PaginatedPosts() {
  const [page, setPage] = useState(1)
  const queryClient = useQueryClient()

  const { data: posts, isLoading, isFetching } = useQuery({
    queryKey: ['posts', page],
    queryFn: () => fetchPosts(page),
    placeholderData: prev => prev, // keep old data while loading
  })

  // Prefetch next page
  useEffect(() => {
    queryClient.prefetchQuery({
      queryKey: ['posts', page + 1],
      queryFn: () => fetchPosts(page + 1),
    })
  }, [page])

  return (
    <div>
      <h2>Page {page} {isFetching && '(updating...)'}</h2>
      {isLoading ? <p>Loading...</p> : posts?.map(p => (
        <p key={p.id}>{p.id}. {p.title}</p>
      ))}
      <button onClick={() => setPage(p => Math.max(1, p - 1)) } disabled={page === 1}>← Prev</button>
      <button onClick={() => setPage(p => p + 1) }>Next →</button>
    </div>
  )
}

Testing with Vitest & React Testing Library

Purpose, From First Principles

Why it exists

Testing exists to protect behavior while the code changes.

What if it did not exist?

Without tests, every refactor requires manual checking and regressions slip in silently.

Learning Ladder

Beginner

Test pure functions first because input and output are obvious.

Intermediate

Test components by interacting the way a user would.

Advanced

Mock network boundaries and test loading/error states.

Mastery

Write tests that describe user-visible behavior, not implementation details.

Practice Ladder - Testing with Vitest & React Testing LibraryGuided Practice

Testing is how you keep confidence as the app grows. Beginners test pure functions first because they are easy to understand. Intermediate learners test components through user behavior. Mastery means writing tests that protect business behavior without locking the implementation in place.

Testing Progression

Unit tests

Validate pure functions like reducers, formatters, and form validators.

Component tests

Render a component, click/type like a user, and assert what appears on screen.

Workflow tests

Cover the important path through routing, loading, saving, and error recovery.

bash
npm install -D vitest @testing-library/react @testing-library/jest-dom @testing-library/user-event jsdom
js — vite.config.js
import { defineConfig } from 'vite'
import react from '@vitejs/plugin-react'

export default defineConfig({
  plugins: [react()],
  test: {
    environment: 'jsdom',
    globals: true,
    setupFiles: './src/setupTests.js',
  }
})
js — src/setupTests.js
import '@testing-library/jest-dom'

Your First Tests

jsx — Counter.test.jsx
import { render, screen } from '@testing-library/react'
import userEvent from '@testing-library/user-event'
import Counter from './Counter'

describe('Counter', () => {
  it('renders with initial count of 0', () => {
    render(<Counter />)
    expect(screen.getByText('Count: 0')).toBeInTheDocument()
  })

  it('increments when + button clicked', async () => {
    const user = userEvent.setup()
    render(<Counter />)

    await user.click(screen.getByRole('button', { name: '+' }))
    expect(screen.getByText('Count: 1')).toBeInTheDocument()
  })

  it('resets to 0', async () => {
    const user = userEvent.setup()
    render(<Counter />)

    await user.click(screen.getByRole('button', { name: '+' }))
    await user.click(screen.getByRole('button', { name: 'Reset' }))
    expect(screen.getByText('Count: 0')).toBeInTheDocument()
  })
})

Testing Forms

jsx
it('submits form with user input', async () => {
  const user = userEvent.setup()
  render(<ContactForm />)

  await user.type(screen.getByPlaceholderText('Your name'), 'Alice')
  await user.type(screen.getByPlaceholderText('Your email'), 'alice@test.com')
  await user.click(screen.getByRole('button', { name: 'Submit' }))

  expect(screen.getByText('Thank you, Alice!')).toBeInTheDocument()
})

Exercise 10.1 — Test Your Todo App Day 10 · Final Exercise

Write a full test suite for the Zustand todo app from Day 8. Cover: rendering empty state, adding a todo, toggling done, deleting, and filtering. Aim for 100% coverage of user interactions.

jsx — TodoApp.test.jsx
import { render, screen } from '@testing-library/react'
import userEvent from '@testing-library/user-event'
import { TodoApp } from './TodoApp'

describe('TodoApp', () => {
  beforeEach(() => {
    // Reset Zustand store between tests
    useTodoStore.setState({ todos: [], filter: 'all' })
  })

  it('shows empty state', () => {
    render(<TodoApp />)
    expect(screen.queryAllByRole('listitem')).toHaveLength(0)
  })

  it('adds a todo', async () => {
    const user = userEvent.setup()
    render(<TodoApp />)

    await user.type(screen.getByPlaceholderText('New todo...'), 'Buy milk')
    await user.click(screen.getByRole('button', { name: 'Add' }))

    expect(screen.getByText('Buy milk')).toBeInTheDocument()
  })

  it('toggles todo done state', async () => {
    useTodoStore.setState({ todos: [{ id: 1, text: 'Test', done: false }] })
    const user = userEvent.setup()
    render(<TodoApp />)

    await user.click(screen.getByRole('checkbox'))
    expect(screen.getByText('Test')).toHaveStyle('text-decoration: line-through')
  })
})

Git Commands

Setup and Config
# Identity
git config --global user.name "Name"
git config --global user.email "e@mail"
# Create / Clone
git init
git clone <url>
# Status
git status
git log --oneline --graph
Stage and Commit
# Stage
git add .
git add <file>
git add -p         # interactive
# Commit
git commit -m "msg"
git commit --amend # fix last commit
# Unstage
git restore --staged <file>
Branches
# List / Create / Switch
git branch
git switch -c feature/x
git switch main
# Merge / Rebase
git merge feature/x
git rebase main
# Delete
git branch -d feature/x
git branch -D feature/x
Remote
# Push / Pull
git push -u origin main
git push
git pull
git fetch origin
# Remotes
git remote -v
git remote add origin <url>
# Stash
git stash
git stash pop
Undo and Reset
# Soft (keep staged)
git reset --soft HEAD~1
# Mixed (keep unstaged)
git reset HEAD~1
# Hard (discard all)
git reset --hard HEAD~1
# Revert safely
git revert <sha>
Useful Tricks
# Pretty log
git log --oneline --graph --all
# Search commits
git log --grep="fix"
# Show changes
git diff
git diff --staged
# Blame
git blame <file>
# Cherry-pick
git cherry-pick <sha>

React Hooks Cheat Sheet

useState
const [val, setVal] = useState(init)
// Primitive update
setVal(newVal)
// Functional (safe)
setVal(prev => prev + 1)
// Object -- spread!
setVal(p => ({...p, key: v}))
useEffect
// Once on mount
useEffect(() => {}, [])
// When dep changes
useEffect(() => {}, [dep])
// With cleanup
useEffect(() => {
  const id = setInterval(fn, 1000)
  return () => clearInterval(id)
}, [])
useReducer
const [state, dispatch] =
  useReducer(reducer, init)
dispatch({ type: 'action', payload })
function reducer(state, action) {
  switch(action.type) {
    case 'action':
      return { ...state }
  }
}
useContext
const Ctx = createContext(default)
// Provide
<Ctx.Provider value={val}>
  {children}
</Ctx.Provider>
// Consume
const val = useContext(Ctx)
useRef
const ref = useRef(null)
// DOM access
<input ref={ref} />
ref.current.focus()
// Mutable value
const timer = useRef(null)
timer.current = setTimeout(fn,1000)
Custom Hook
function useMyHook(param) {
  const [data, setData] = useState(null)
  useEffect(() => {
    // effect logic
  }, [param])
  return { data }
}
const { data } = useMyHook(x)

npm Package Reference

The most important packages in the React ecosystem.

Core

react + react-dom
npm install react react-dom

The core React library plus the DOM renderer. These always go together.

Essential
vite + plugin-react
npm create vite@latest

Lightning-fast build tool and dev server with HMR. Replaces Create React App.

Essential

Routing

react-router-dom

Declarative routing. BrowserRouter, Routes, Route, Link, NavLink, useNavigate, useParams, useSearchParams, Outlet for nested routes.

Essential
@tanstack/router
npm install @tanstack/react-router

Type-safe file-based routing. More powerful, steeper curve. The emerging standard.

State Management

zustand
npm install zustand

Minimal, fast global state. No boilerplate, no mandatory providers. Middleware for devtools and persistence.

Recommended
jotai
npm install jotai

Atomic state: atoms are tiny pieces of state. Derived atoms automatically update. Zero boilerplate.

@reduxjs/toolkit
npm install @reduxjs/toolkit

Modern Redux with createSlice, immer, RTK Query. Best for large teams needing strict structure.

immer
npm install immer

Write mutating code that produces immutable results. Used inside Zustand and Redux Toolkit.

Data Fetching

@tanstack/react-query
npm install @tanstack/react-query

Server-state gold standard: caching, background refetch, mutations, infinite queries, optimistic updates, devtools.

Essential
axios
npm install axios

HTTP client with interceptors, auto JSON parsing, and better error handling than native fetch.

Recommended

Styling

tailwindcss
npm install -D tailwindcss

Utility-first CSS. Style with class names directly in JSX. Responsive, dark mode, all built in.

Recommended
clsx
npm install clsx

Tiny utility for conditional class names. Essential with Tailwind and dynamic states.

framer-motion
npm install framer-motion

Production-ready animations. Declarative, gestures, scroll effects, layout animations.

Forms

react-hook-form
npm install react-hook-form

Performant forms via uncontrolled inputs. useForm, register, handleSubmit, formState. Pairs with Zod for validation.

Recommended
zod
npm install zod

TypeScript-first schema validation. Define shapes for forms, API responses, env variables. Excellent error messages.

Testing

vitest
npm install -D vitest

Vite-native unit testing. Jest-compatible API, much faster. Use with jsdom for browser simulation.

Recommended
@testing-library/react
npm install -D @testing-library/react

Query the DOM the way users do: by role, text, label. Discourages testing implementation details.

Essential
msw
npm install -D msw

Mock Service Worker. Intercepts real network requests in tests and the browser. Best API mocking approach.

Reference

Glossary of Terms

Every important term defined in plain English.

Git and Version Control

Repository
A folder tracked by Git containing your project files and their entire history. Can be local (on your machine) or remote (GitHub).
Commit
A saved snapshot of your project at a point in time. Each commit has a unique SHA hash, a message, an author, and a timestamp.
Branch
An independent pointer to a commit, enabling parallel development lines. The default branch is called main. Branches are lightweight and fast.
Merge
Integrating changes from one branch into another. Creates a merge commit with two parent commits, preserving full history.
Rebase
Replaying commits from one branch on top of another. Produces a clean, linear history but rewrites commit SHAs — never on shared branches.
Pull Request (PR)
A GitHub proposal to merge one branch into another. The primary mechanism for code review in team workflows.
Stash
Temporarily shelves uncommitted changes so you can switch context, then restore them later with git stash pop.
HEAD
A pointer to the current commit — usually the tip of the active branch. HEAD~1 means one commit before current.
Origin
The default name for the remote repository, usually on GitHub. Just an alias for the remote URL.
Fast-forward
A merge that just moves the branch pointer forward when there is no divergent history. Creates no merge commit.

React and JavaScript

Component
A reusable, self-contained piece of UI. In modern React, a component is a JavaScript function that returns JSX.
JSX
JavaScript XML — a syntax extension that lets you write HTML-like code in JavaScript, compiled to React.createElement() calls by Vite or Babel.
Props
Short for properties. Read-only data passed from a parent to a child component. Think of them as function arguments for components.
State
Mutable data that belongs to a component. When state changes, React automatically re-renders the component and its children.
Hook
A function starting with use that hooks into React features. Must be called at the top level of a component — never inside conditions or loops.
Side Effect
Anything that reaches outside the component: API calls, DOM manipulation, timers, subscriptions. Managed with useEffect.
Virtual DOM
React's in-memory representation of the real DOM. React diffs old vs new virtual DOM trees to compute minimal real DOM changes needed.
Reconciliation
The algorithm React uses to diff the previous and new virtual DOM trees and efficiently update only what changed in the real DOM.
Lifting State Up
Moving shared state to the nearest common ancestor of the components that need it, then passing data down as props and callbacks.
Prop Drilling
Passing props through many intermediate components that do not use them. Solved by Context API or global state managers like Zustand.
Controlled Component
A form input whose value is driven by React state via value and onChange. React is the single source of truth.
Memoization
Caching expensive computations. useMemo memoizes values, useCallback memoizes functions, React.memo prevents component re-renders.
SPA
Single-Page Application. The browser loads one HTML page and JavaScript dynamically updates the UI without full reloads. React Router handles navigation.
HMR
Hot Module Replacement. Vite updates changed modules in the browser instantly without a full reload, preserving application state.
Code Splitting
Breaking your bundle into smaller chunks loaded on demand. React.lazy() and dynamic import() enable route-level code splitting.

Tooling

Vite
A modern build tool using native ES modules for near-instant dev server startup. Dramatically faster than webpack-based tools.
npm
Node Package Manager. Bundled with Node.js. Installs, manages, and publishes JavaScript packages from the npm registry.
ESLint
Static analysis that finds problems in JavaScript code — undeclared variables, missing hook dependencies, anti-patterns.
Prettier
Opinionated code formatter that enforces consistent style (indentation, quotes, semicolons) automatically across the whole codebase.
Tree Shaking
Build optimization that removes unused code from your bundle. Works with ES module imports — only what you import gets included.

Git Advanced

Git Workflows & GitHub

How real teams work: feature branches, pull requests, CI/CD, releases.

GitHub Flow

  1. Create a branch from main for each feature or fix. Name it clearly: feature/user-auth, fix/login-crash.

  2. Commit often with small, atomic conventional commits. Each commit should be independently understandable.

  3. Open a Pull Request early — as a draft if not ready. Write a clear description of what and why, not just how.

  4. Request code review. Teammates comment. You push fixes in response. GitHub tracks all activity inline on the diff.

  5. Merge once approved and CI passes. Use Squash and Merge for a clean main branch history.

  6. Deploy automatically — Vercel and Netlify watch main and deploy on every merge.

Merge vs. Rebase

AspectMergeRebase
HistoryPreserves exact history, adds merge commitRewrites history, linear result
SafetyAlways safeNever rebase shared/public branches
ReadabilityCan get noisy with many branchesClean, linear log
Best forMerging feature into mainUpdating feature branch from main
bash — Interactive Rebase
# Squash last 3 commits into 1
git rebase -i HEAD~3
# In editor: change 2nd/3rd 'pick' to 's'
# Write a clean combined commit message

# Update feature branch from main
git switch feature/my-feature
git fetch origin
git rebase origin/main

# Force-push rebased branch (your branch only!)
git push --force-with-lease

GitHub Actions CI/CD

yaml — .github/workflows/ci.yml
name: CI

on:
  push:
    branches: [ main ]
  pull_request:
    branches: [ main ]

jobs:
  test:
    runs-on: ubuntu-latest
    steps:
      - uses: actions/checkout@v4
      - uses: actions/setup-node@v4
        with:
          node-version: '20'
          cache: 'npm'
      - run: npm ci
      - run: npm run lint
      - run: npm test -- --run
      - run: npm run build

Common Git Mistakes and Fixes

Committed to wrong branch

git cherry-pick <sha> on the correct branch, then git reset HEAD~1 on the wrong one.

Deleted branch accidentally

git reflog to find the last SHA, then git switch -c recovery <sha>.

Pushed sensitive secrets

Use git-filter-repo to purge from history, force-push, then immediately rotate all exposed credentials.

Merge conflict on pull

Open conflicted files, find markers, resolve manually, then git add . && git commit.

Committed node_modules

Add to .gitignore, then git rm -r --cached node_modules and commit the removal.

Need file from old commit

git checkout <sha> -- path/to/file restores just that file from any commit.

Advanced

Advanced React Patterns

useMemo, useCallback, compound components, error boundaries, code splitting, and React 18 concurrent features.

useMemo and useCallback

These hooks memoize values and functions to prevent unnecessary recalculations and re-renders. Use them only after profiling reveals actual performance issues.

jsx
import { useMemo, useCallback, memo } from 'react'

// useMemo: recompute only when dependency changes
const sorted = useMemo(
  () => [...items].sort((a, b) => a.name.localeCompare(b.name)),
  [items]
)

// useCallback: stable function reference for child props
const handleClick = useCallback((id) => {
  onItemClick(id)
}, [onItemClick])

// React.memo: skip re-render when props unchanged
const ExpensiveChild = memo(({ data }) => (
  <div>{data.map(d => <Item key={d.id} {...d} />)}</div>
))
Warning: Premature Optimization
Only apply useMemo, useCallback, and React.memo when you have measured a real performance problem. They add complexity and can hurt performance if misused.

Compound Component Pattern

jsx
import { createContext, useContext, useState } from 'react'

const AccordionCtx = createContext(null)

function Accordion({ children }) {
  const [open, setOpen] = useState(null)
  return (
    <AccordionCtx.Provider value={{ open, setOpen }}>
      <div>{children}</div>
    </AccordionCtx.Provider>
  )
}

function AccordionItem({ id, title, children }) {
  const { open, setOpen } = useContext(AccordionCtx)
  const isOpen = open === id
  return (
    <div>
      <button onClick={() => setOpen(isOpen ? null : id)}>
        {title} {isOpen ? '▲' : '▼'}
      </button>
      {isOpen && <div>{children}</div>}
    </div>
  )
}
Accordion.Item = AccordionItem

// Elegant, readable usage:
<Accordion>
  <Accordion.Item id="1" title="What is React?">A UI library.</Accordion.Item>
  <Accordion.Item id="2" title="What is JSX?">HTML in JS.</Accordion.Item>
</Accordion>

Error Boundaries

bash + jsx
npm install react-error-boundary

import { ErrorBoundary } from 'react-error-boundary'

function ErrorFallback({ error, resetErrorBoundary }) {
  return (
    <div role="alert">
      <h2>Something went wrong</h2>
      <pre>{error.message}</pre>
      <button onClick={resetErrorBoundary}>Try again</button>
    </div>
  )
}

<ErrorBoundary FallbackComponent={ErrorFallback}>
  <App />
</ErrorBoundary>

Code Splitting with lazy()

jsx
import { lazy, Suspense } from 'react'

// Downloaded only when the route is visited
const Dashboard = lazy(() => import('./pages/Dashboard'))
const Settings  = lazy(() => import('./pages/Settings'))

function App() {
  return (
    <Suspense fallback={<p>Loading...</p>}>
      <Routes>
        <Route path="/" element={<Dashboard />} />
        <Route path="/settings" element={<Settings />} />
      </Routes>
    </Suspense>
  )
}

React 18: useTransition

jsx
import { useTransition } from 'react'

function SearchPage() {
  const [query, setQuery] = useState('')
  const [results, setResults] = useState([])
  const [isPending, startTransition] = useTransition()

  const handleSearch = (e) => {
    const val = e.target.value
    setQuery(val)            // urgent: update input immediately
    startTransition(() => {
      setResults(search(val)) // non-urgent: can be interrupted
    })
  }

  return (
    <div>
      <input value={query} onChange={handleSearch} />
      {isPending && <span>Updating...</span>}
      {results.map(r => <div key={r.id}>{r.name}</div>)}
    </div>
  )
}
Exercise — Infinite Scroll with useInfiniteQueryAdvanced Challenge

Build an infinite-scrolling post list. Fetch 10 posts per page from JSONPlaceholder. Use useInfiniteQuery and IntersectionObserver to load the next page when the user scrolls to the bottom.

jsx
import { useInfiniteQuery } from '@tanstack/react-query'
import { useRef, useEffect } from 'react'
import axios from 'axios'

const fetchPosts = async ({ pageParam = 1 }) => {
  const { data } = await axios.get(
    `https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/posts?_page=${pageParam}&_limit=10`
  )
  return { data, nextPage: data.length === 10 ? pageParam + 1 : null }
}

function InfiniteList() {
  const { data, fetchNextPage, hasNextPage, isFetchingNextPage } =
    useInfiniteQuery({
      queryKey: ['posts'],
      queryFn: fetchPosts,
      getNextPageParam: (last) => last.nextPage,
    })

  const bottomRef = useRef(null)

  useEffect(() => {
    const obs = new IntersectionObserver(([entry]) => {
      if (entry.isIntersecting && hasNextPage) fetchNextPage()
    })
    if (bottomRef.current) obs.observe(bottomRef.current)
    return () => obs.disconnect()
  }, [hasNextPage, fetchNextPage])

  return (
    <div>
      {data?.pages.flatMap(p => p.data).map(post => (
        <p key={post.id}><strong>{post.title}</strong></p>
      ))}
      <div ref={bottomRef}>
        {isFetchingNextPage ? 'Loading...' : hasNextPage ? 'Scroll for more' : 'All done!'}
      </div>
    </div>
  )
}

Core Store

js -- store/useTaskStore.js
import { create } from 'zustand'
import { persist } from 'zustand/middleware'

const useTaskStore = create(persist(
  (set, get) => ({
    tasks: [],
    filter: { status: 'all', priority: 'all', search: '' },

    addTask: (task) => set(s => ({
      tasks: [...s.tasks, {
        id: crypto.randomUUID(),
        createdAt: new Date().toISOString(),
        done: false, ...task
      }]
    })),

    updateTask: (id, changes) => set(s => ({
      tasks: s.tasks.map(t => t.id === id ? { ...t, ...changes } : t)
    })),

    deleteTask: (id) => set(s => ({
      tasks: s.tasks.filter(t => t.id !== id)
    })),

    toggleTask: (id) => set(s => ({
      tasks: s.tasks.map(t =>
        t.id === id ? { ...t, done: !t.done } : t
      )
    })),

    setFilter: (key, val) =>
      set(s => ({ filter: { ...s.filter, [key]: val } })),

    getFiltered: () => {
      const { tasks, filter } = get()
      return tasks
        .filter(t => filter.status === 'all' ||
          (filter.status === 'done' ? t.done : !t.done))
        .filter(t => filter.priority === 'all' ||
          t.priority === filter.priority)
        .filter(t => t.title.toLowerCase()
          .includes(filter.search.toLowerCase()))
    }
  }),
  { name: 'taskflow-store' }
))

Best Practices

Performance & Best Practices

Write React code that scales: performance, accessibility, security, folder structure.

React Performance Profiling

jsx
// 1. Use React DevTools Profiler tab to record renders
// 2. Find components that re-render unnecessarily
// 3. Apply fixes — measure again to confirm improvement

// Wrap component in React.memo to skip re-renders
// when props haven't changed
const ExpensiveChart = React.memo(({ data }) => {
  // heavy render logic
  return <canvas />
}, (prevProps, nextProps) => {
  // Custom comparison: return true to SKIP re-render
  return prevProps.data.id === nextProps.data.id
})

// Expensive calculation — cache with useMemo
const stats = useMemo(() => {
  return data.reduce((acc, item) => ({
    total: acc.total + item.value,
    avg: (acc.total + item.value) / (acc.count + 1),
    count: acc.count + 1
  }), { total: 0, avg: 0, count: 0 })
}, [data])

Accessibility (a11y) Essentials

Why Accessibility Matters
Accessible apps work for everyone — people with visual, motor, or cognitive disabilities, users on keyboards only, and assistive technology users. Also: it improves SEO.
jsx
// Always use semantic HTML
<button>Click me</button>  // ✅ not <div onClick>
<nav>, <main>, <header>, <footer>  // ✅ landmark elements

// Labels for form inputs
<label htmlFor="email">Email</label>
<input id="email" type="email" />

// ARIA attributes when semantic HTML isn't enough
<button
  aria-label="Close modal"
  aria-expanded={isOpen}
  aria-controls="menu-list"
>✕</button>

// Images need alt text
<img src="logo.png" alt="Company logo" />
<img src="decoration.svg" alt="" />  // decorative = empty alt

// Focus management for modals
useEffect(() => {
  if (isOpen) firstFocusableRef.current?.focus()
}, [isOpen])

Security Best Practices

🚫 XSS Warning
Never use dangerouslySetInnerHTML with user-supplied content. React escapes JSX content automatically — trust the framework.
jsx
// ❌ XSS vulnerability
<div dangerouslySetInnerHTML={{ __html: userInput }} />

// ✅ React escapes this automatically
<div>{userInput}</div>

// ❌ Never put secrets in frontend code
const API_KEY = 'sk-abc123'  // visible to anyone in DevTools

// ✅ Secrets belong on the server
// Frontend only uses VITE_ prefixed public config
const BASE_URL = import.meta.env.VITE_API_URL

// ✅ Validate/sanitize before sending to server
import DOMPurify from 'dompurify'
const safe = DOMPurify.sanitize(htmlString)

Code Quality Checklist

  • Components are small and focused on one job
  • No business logic in JSX — extract to hooks or utils
  • Keys are stable, unique IDs — not array indices
  • All useEffect dependencies are declared
  • Async effects handle cancellation with cleanup
  • Error states are handled — no silent failures
  • Loading states are displayed to the user
  • Forms use labels, required fields, accessible errors
  • Images have descriptive alt text
  • No console.log left in production code
  • Environment variables use VITE_ prefix (not secrets)
  • ESLint passes with 0 errors or warnings
  • Tests cover the main user interactions
Debugging

Debugging React Apps

Find and fix bugs faster with the right tools and mental models.

React DevTools

Install the React Developer Tools browser extension (Chrome/Firefox). It adds two panels to DevTools:

Components Tab

Inspect the component tree, view props and state, trigger state changes manually, and highlight what re-rendered.

Profiler Tab

Record a session and see exactly which components rendered, why, and how long each render took.

Common React Bugs & Fixes

jsx — Common Bugs
// BUG 1: Stale closure in async effect
useEffect(() => {
  fetchData().then(data => {
    setItems([...items, ...data])  // ❌ stale 'items'
    setItems(prev => [...prev, ...data])  // ✅ always fresh
  })
}, [])  // Missing 'items' dep warning from ESLint

// BUG 2: Object/array in deps causes infinite loop
useEffect(() => {
  fetchUser(options)
}, [options])  // ❌ new object reference every render!

// Fix: memoize the object
const memoOptions = useMemo(() => ({ id: userId }), [userId])
useEffect(() => { fetchUser(memoOptions) }, [memoOptions])

// BUG 3: Setting state on unmounted component
useEffect(() => {
  let mounted = true
  fetchData().then(data => {
    if (mounted) setData(data)  // ✅ safe
  })
  return () => { mounted = false }  // cleanup
}, [])

// BUG 4: Missing key causes wrong component reuse
{items.map((item, i) => <Input key={i} />)}     // ❌ unstable
{items.map(item => <Input key={item.id} />)}     // ✅

// BUG 5: useState not updating immediately (async)
setCount(5)
console.log(count)  // ❌ still old value — state updates are async
// React batches updates. Use useEffect to react to changes.

Debugging Tools Checklist

console.log / console.table

The fastest way to inspect values. console.table(array) is great for arrays of objects.

React DevTools Profiler

Profile renders to find performance bottlenecks. Look for components that render too often.

Network Tab

Inspect all API requests, status codes, request/response payloads. Filter by XHR/Fetch.

VS Code Debugger

Set breakpoints in JSX and step through React component code. Add debugger statement to trigger.

why-did-you-render

npm package that logs why components re-render to the console. Great for finding unnecessary renders.

Zustand DevTools

Connect Zustand stores to Redux DevTools. See every action dispatched and the state before/after.

Debugging useEffect Issues

jsx
// Symptom: Effect runs too many times
// Diagnosis: Log the dependencies
useEffect(() => {
  console.log('effect ran, deps:', { userId, options })
  fetchUser(userId)
}, [userId, options])

// Symptom: Infinite loop
// Most likely cause: object/array/function in deps
// Fix: useMemo for objects, useCallback for functions

// Symptom: Effect never runs
// Check: dependency array — is [] correct?
// Check: is the component even mounting?
useEffect(() => {
  console.log('mounted!')
  return () => console.log('unmounted!')
}, [])
React StrictMode Double-Invocation
In development, React StrictMode intentionally runs effects twice (mount → unmount → mount) to help you find bugs from missing cleanup. This is normal and only happens in dev. Your cleanup function must properly undo the effect.
Exercise — Debug This ComponentDebugging · Exercise

The following component has 3 bugs. Find and fix them all: (1) it causes an infinite loop, (2) it has a stale closure, (3) it leaks a timer. Read the code carefully before looking at the solution.

jsx — Buggy Component
function BuggyTimer({ userId }) {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0)
  const [user, setUser] = useState(null)

  // Bug 1: infinite loop
  useEffect(() => {
    setUser({ id: userId, name: 'Test' })
  }, [{ id: userId }])  // new object every render

  // Bug 2: stale closure + Bug 3: timer leak
  useEffect(() => {
    setInterval(() => {
      setCount(count + 1)  // stale count
    }, 1000)
    // no cleanup!
  }, [])

  return <div>{user?.name}: {count}</div>
}
jsx — Fixed
function FixedTimer({ userId }) {
  const [count, setCount] = useState(0)
  const [user, setUser] = useState(null)

  // Fix 1: use primitive userId as dependency, not a new object
  useEffect(() => {
    setUser({ id: userId, name: 'Test' })
  }, [userId])  // ✅ stable primitive

  // Fix 2 and 3: functional update + cleanup
  useEffect(() => {
    const id = setInterval(() => {
      setCount(prev => prev + 1)  // ✅ no stale closure
    }, 1000)
    return () => clearInterval(id)  // ✅ cleanup prevents leak
  }, [])  // still empty — effect doesn't use count

  return <div>{user?.name}: {count}</div>
}
Next Steps

TypeScript with React

Add static typing to React for fewer bugs, better autocomplete, and self-documenting code.

Setup

bash
# Create a new Vite + React + TypeScript project
npm create vite@latest my-app -- --template react-ts

# Add TypeScript to existing project
npm install -D typescript @types/react @types/react-dom

Typing Components and Props

tsx
// Define prop types with an interface
interface ButtonProps {
  label: string
  variant?: 'primary' | 'secondary' | 'danger'
  onClick: () => void
  disabled?: boolean
  children?: React.ReactNode
}

function Button({ label, variant = 'primary', onClick, disabled }: ButtonProps) {
  return (
    <button
      className={`btn btn-${variant}`}
      onClick={onClick}
      disabled={disabled}
    >
      {label}
    </button>
  )
}

// Typing useState
const [user, setUser] = useState<User | null>(null)
const [items, setItems] = useState<Item[]>([])

// Typing events
const handleChange = (e: React.ChangeEvent<HTMLInputElement>) => {
  setValue(e.target.value)
}

const handleSubmit = (e: React.FormEvent<HTMLFormElement>) => {
  e.preventDefault()
}

// Typing useRef
const inputRef = useRef<HTMLInputElement>(null)

// Typing children
interface CardProps {
  title: string
  children: React.ReactNode   // any valid JSX
}

// Typing custom hooks
function useFetch<T>(url: string): { data: T | null; loading: boolean; error: string | null } {
  const [data, setData] = useState<T | null>(null)
  // ...
  return { data, loading, error }
}

Typing Zustand Stores

tsx — store/useCounterStore.ts
import { create } from 'zustand'

interface CounterState {
  count: number
  increment: () => void
  decrement: () => void
  reset: () => void
}

const useCounterStore = create<CounterState>((set) => ({
  count: 0,
  increment: () => set(s => ({ count: s.count + 1 })),
  decrement: () => set(s => ({ count: s.count - 1 })),
  reset: () => set({ count: 0 }),
}))

export default useCounterStore

Deeper Topics to Explore Next

TypeScript

Add static types to all your React code. The combination of React + TypeScript is the industry standard for production apps.

Next.js

React framework with server-side rendering, file-based routing, API routes, image optimization, and edge functions.

Testing (Advanced)

Mock Service Worker (msw) for API mocking, Playwright for end-to-end tests, 100% coverage mindset.

React Query (Advanced)

Optimistic updates, infinite queries, query invalidation strategies, background sync.

Accessibility

ARIA patterns, keyboard navigation, focus management, axe-core for automated a11y testing.

Performance

Web Vitals, code splitting, lazy loading images, virtualization with react-window for large lists.

Monorepos

Turborepo or Nx for managing multiple apps and packages in a single repository.

Storybook

Develop and document UI components in isolation. Industry standard for design systems.

Projects to Build for Your Portfolio

Real-Time Chat
